<span id="freeTextContainer8903121189841123759">Abbey's best friend Kristen dies or so the whole town believes, because the body hasn't been found yet. She finds consolation in doing the things she would've done were Kristen with her. Hanging out at Sleepy Hollow's cemetery. Talking to (dead) Mr Irving. Looking for new things. There she also meets <s>Casper</s> Caspian, who seems to be more than meets the eye.<br/><br/>I read 3/4 of the book and skimmed through the rest. The pacing of the book was kind of off. Slow. Not that much suspense. Mrs Verday must've </span>
  <span id="freeText8903121189841123759" style="display:none">Abbey's best friend Kristen dies or so the whole town believes, because the body hasn't been found yet. She finds consolation in doing the things she would've done were Kristen with her. Hanging out at Sleepy Hollow's cemetery. Talking to (dead) Mr Irving. Looking for new things. There she also meets <s>Casper</s> Caspian, who seems to be more than meets the eye.<br /><br />I read 3/4 of the book and skimmed through the rest. The pacing of the book was kind of off. Slow. Not that much suspense. Mrs Verday must've thought the suspense she created through the <i>mysterious</i> <s>Casper</s> Caspian and the unsolved case of Kristen's whereabouts were enough. Which it sadly weren't. The idea itself wasn't original either, - entwining a classic (<i>Irving's Sleepy Hollow</i>) with the author's own story. I guess the potential was there, but it wasn't tastefully done. So, there you go!</span>

<div id="review_68136089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68136089" />
    <a title="Krystle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle"><img alt="Krystle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403921272p2/2639204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68136089?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystle" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle">Krystle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68136089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15255733791370517430">I picked up this book because I was intrigued by the incorporation of The Legend of Sleepy Hollow into the story and the very striking cover. Sadly, picking a book mainly on the merits of its cover was not a smart thing to do.<br/><br/>It was a chore to read this book. Most of this story revolves around the day to day where it seems like the plot was nowhere to be found, nor was it actually moving forward. I couldn’t help but scream to myself, “what is the point of all this!” Her life consists of Caspian,</span>
  <span id="freeText15255733791370517430" style="display:none">I picked up this book because I was intrigued by the incorporation of The Legend of Sleepy Hollow into the story and the very striking cover. Sadly, picking a book mainly on the merits of its cover was not a smart thing to do.<br /><br />It was a chore to read this book. Most of this story revolves around the day to day where it seems like the plot was nowhere to be found, nor was it actually moving forward. I couldn’t help but scream to myself, “what is the point of all this!” Her life consists of Caspian, Caspian, and nothing but Caspian. It was like she was consumed by him. Beh! And for that the romance felt extremely rushed, lacked chemistry, and didn’t feel at all plausible.<br /><br />The writing for this story varied from decent, poor, to annoying, and usually they could all be found in the same chapter. I’m guessing if I had to make a comparison it reminds me of Beautiful Creatures, just not as somber of a mood and with less of an obvious plot. There were lots of repetitions and the use of the word very. Bleh.<br /><br />And the climax of this book was not satisfactory at all. The huge big reveal left me going, “what you couldn’t have done that about 250 pages earlier?” And not all the plot points were wrapped up either. Who the heck is this person her friend Kristen was dating? It didn’t even delve into that other than “maybe I should be happy not knowing”. HUH?<br /><br />On the plus side, I liked how Abbey made perfumes and all the intricate details in the choice of ingredients, scents, and the process she used to create them. The book made an effort to showcase real grief at someone losing their best friend; it didn’t just go away in the span of a few chapters. The repercussions lasted almost throughout the book, a much more realistic depiction. But was it done well? Eh, that’s up for debate.<br /><br />The best thing is that the spacing between lines is huge, so you’d be able to read through it fast. Interesting premise and cover but lacked in actual development and execution.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15255733791370517430" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8569953911291126371">Ah- I- no- My god- SO BAD!<br/><br/>I am honestly astounded how BAD this book was. I was really looking forward to reading it for some reason, but this book was seriously the biggest let down I've ever read.<br/>I'm really mad, so instead of ranting, I'm going to list. Yes, lists are my friends.<br/>-Main character with almost NO personality.<br/>-Main character with only the trait of BLOODY ANNOYING AND SLAP WORTHY<br/>-Main character trying to be distinguished by one tiny thing that just DOES NOT WORK<br/>-Main character random</span>
  <span id="freeText8569953911291126371" style="display:none">Ah- I- no- My god- SO BAD!<br /><br />I am honestly astounded how BAD this book was. I was really looking forward to reading it for some reason, but this book was seriously the biggest let down I've ever read.<br />I'm really mad, so instead of ranting, I'm going to list. Yes, lists are my friends.<br />-Main character with almost NO personality.<br />-Main character with only the trait of BLOODY ANNOYING AND SLAP WORTHY<br />-Main character trying to be distinguished by one tiny thing that just DOES NOT WORK<br />-Main character randomly throwing up, having breakdowns and grinning when she just got rejected<br />-Main character completely oblivious<br />-Main character supposedly 'smart' when she sounds like the dumbest person on the planet<br />-Love interest so Edward-like it was freaking soul crushing<br />-Love interest WAY too dramatic and over the top<br />-Love interest with no personality besides 'the love interest'<br />-I guessed what the love interest was like halfway through the book<br />-Main character's parents either ignorant to the and/or ignore child, or overbearing/terrible at parenting/bipolar<br />-So totally generic the gun started looking enticing, eg. cemeteries, friends dying, second 'nice' love interest, the underdog, total wuss, ghosts<br />-Book draaaaaaaaaaaagged out so much I literally nearly stopped reading it<br /><br />As you can see, I could go on forever. But I won't put you through that.<br /><br />One of the many, many worst parts was the fact I was so excited about this book, that I got this one PLUS the sequel out, and now I can't stand the sight of either. I'm not even going to give the second book a chance, I don't care if it's a thousand times better, it still WON'T BE GOOD!<br /><br />This book is seriously in the running for the worst book I've ever read and I commend anyone who has also suffered through these long, drawn out, insufferable pages.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1393879228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2301089099435110829">Actually 1.5⭐️<br/>When I read a book I want to get emotionally involved. I want to be taken on an adventure, get frustrated, sad, angry or explode with happiness... I felt nothing but boredom.<br/>This story didn't peak till the last 30 pages or so...It was stagnant for 480 pages! And what disappointed me even more is that I knew what was coming, so it wasn't even a surprise for me :(<br/>The name of the book is The Hollow, where is the thrill? Where is the horror? The setting is Sleepy Hollow for crying out </span>
  <span id="freeText2301089099435110829" style="display:none">Actually 1.5⭐️<br />When I read a book I want to get emotionally involved. I want to be taken on an adventure, get frustrated, sad, angry or explode with happiness... I felt nothing but boredom.<br />This story didn't peak till the last 30 pages or so...It was stagnant for 480 pages! And what disappointed me even more is that I knew what was coming, so it wasn't even a surprise for me :(<br />The name of the book is The Hollow, where is the thrill? Where is the horror? The setting is Sleepy Hollow for crying out loud! The only morbidity represented was a cemetery and nothing happened! She just visited it over and over again and that's it! <br /><br />The romance was dull, as Caspian's character was barely a character to begin with. He was vague and barely had presence. I knew he had a secret, but it was just a flop for me when it was revealed :/ <br />I felt like I read 470 pages of teenage angst followed by 30- something pages of barely there 'suspense'.<br /><br />I hate to be bashing another novel in one month. Actually, I hate giving bad reviews at all! But I am just being honest and this is only MY opinion....I'm sorry to all who loves this book. <br />I initially thought that this would be more suitable for 12-15 year olds, but I've read some middle grade books and the standard far exceeds what this book offered.<br /><br />In the end, I might not be continuing with this trilogy and that is a very hard thing to say because It just makes me sad when a story's potential is destroyed. :(</span>
  <a data-text-id="2301089099435110829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_69981145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69981145" />
    <a title="Allybal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2480225-allybal"><img alt="Allybal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483703597p2/2480225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69981145?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allybal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allybal" href="/user/show/2480225-allybal">Allybal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2480225-allybal?shelf=vampires-and-other-night-creatures">vampires-and-other-night-creatures</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69981145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5014621399913740991">"...This sequestered glen has long been known by the name of Sleepy Hollow."<br/><br/><br/>When I received The Hollow in the mail I nearly threw my other reading selections aside, their bookmarks noting my reality of being rather far from completion, and I happily welcomed this exciting, inviting take on an old classic.<br/><br/>You are greeted by obviously beautiful cover art, and a well chosen font style but then you open the rather large book to see nearly 500 pages of a much larger then necessary font.(Oh, the waste</span>
  <span id="freeText5014621399913740991" style="display:none">"...This sequestered glen has long been known by the name of Sleepy Hollow."<br /><br /><br />When I received The Hollow in the mail I nearly threw my other reading selections aside, their bookmarks noting my reality of being rather far from completion, and I happily welcomed this exciting, inviting take on an old classic.<br /><br />You are greeted by obviously beautiful cover art, and a well chosen font style but then you open the rather large book to see nearly 500 pages of a much larger then necessary font.(Oh, the waste of paper!) The first chapter in about 8 pages, but it takes less then two minutes to read... it's just a little unnecessary.(Even if it's aimed at younger 'tweens' they can still read a more moderately sized type.)<br /><br />Any-who, I finished The Hollow in two long, uninspired days to be left feeling entirely disappointed and with more then a few question marks looming overhead.<br /><br />Abbey and Kristen have a strange obsession with their hometown, Sleepy Hollow and the famous Legend that is derived from it. Which ultimately leaves them unpopular, and painfully strange.<br /><br />When Abbey meets Caspian, a dark, mysterious brooding type in the cemetery she frequents, a rather alarming crush occurs, or as we are to believe a relationship is formed. Which of course works out beautifully to help distract our misfit Abbey from the recent death of her best and only friend, Kristen.<br /><br />Our heroine, Abbey is original sure, in that archetypal 'loner-girl' kind of way that is customary to these human/supernatural relationship central tales.<br />Although I will say that her passion of creating perfumes was rather intriguing,... at first, that quickly became tired with her prolonged explanations of their individual scents and composition.<br />Author Tip: Don't focus so long on certain things that you cannot control. Reading a book cannot convey real scent, the attempt at creating a real sensation is nice, but not possible. Overall it becomes redundant, then frustrating.. I would love to be able to smell Kristen's very original perfume, or Caspian's that smells like delicious snicker-doodle cookies, but hey this is reality and not smell-o-vision book edition.<br /><br />Which isn't to allude that I dislike description, it's just that overall I find, Verday hasn't quite grasped the most enjoyable way for the reader to really see her stories. Pages and pages focus on mundane tasks that have no real place or importance in the plot and aren't even slightly entertaining. Abbey working for her uncle, Abbey walking through her cemetery routine, Abbey cooking, Abbey making perfume, Abbey whining over her non-relationship with Caspian, Abbey whining about how much she misses Kristen....<br /><br />Really, Abbey just does a lot of whining.<br /><br />Not to mention, Caspian isn't very drool-worthy. He seems completely indifferent to Abbey most of the time, and by the end I find myself almost forgetting anything he's done only chapters before and even worse caring if their 'relationship' will work out.<br /><br />Maybe I'm just hypercritical because it's been a few years since high school for me, maybe I've crossed over that bridge and can't really connect because that part of my life is over... but I enjoy plenty of young adult novels without feeling so completely void of any and all REAL emotion. That tends to be the best part of these types of stories, their ability to transport us all back to a different point in our lives, with sweeping emotions and stereotypical but entertaining characters and situations.<br /><br /><br />The most upsetting element of this whole thing too, is the climax and resolution are thrown together so sloppily in the last few chapters it all barely makes sense. It really is a great idea, it just needed a lot more work.... and a real plot.<br /><br />Oh, and I still can't find a moral to the story.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5014621399913740991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5Hl0jSIY7jJXcd8fBsN/zUvIeRQJhz+ga+CdQKXBQiAvjO5WJ4mPHISA/UXQMzfpuRe1cpYpMOE6xV91ni4Edg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OfvJi3yvcW4fZsLuCdV9XqXwxgR+kZi6fmWkmSubErjyDlNQeT4QQMyX4LTfJTV6Vy8KYuE/l/svQGasEHRU7g==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9486906731820264674">Jessica Verday is the New York Times bestselling author of The Hollow Trilogy, published by Simon & Schuster/Simon Pulse. She wrote the first draft of THE HOLLOW by hand, using thirteen spiral-bound notebooks and fifteen black pens. The first draft of THE HAUNTED took fifteen spiral-bound notebooks and twenty black pens. THE HIDDEN took too many notebooks and too many pens to count. Find out more </span>
  <span id="freeText9486906731820264674" style="display:none">Jessica Verday is the New York Times bestselling author of The Hollow Trilogy, published by Simon &amp; Schuster/Simon Pulse. She wrote the first draft of THE HOLLOW by hand, using thirteen spiral-bound notebooks and fifteen black pens. The first draft of THE HAUNTED took fifteen spiral-bound notebooks and twenty black pens. THE HIDDEN took too many notebooks and too many pens to count. Find out more at jessicaverday.com.</span>
